A replicated log can be\\n450:     used by other systems as a primitive for implementing other distributed systems in the <a href=\\\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_machine_replication\\\">state-machine style</a>.\\n451:     <p>\\n452: \",\"endLine\":452,\"startLine\":449},{\"content\":\"446: \\n447:     <h4><a id=\\\"design_replicatedlog\\\" href=\\\"#design_replicatedlog\\\">Replicated Logs: Quorums, ISRs, and State Machines (Oh my!)</a></h4>\\n448: \\n449: \",\"endLine\":449,\"startLine\":446},{\"content\":\"493:     \\\"stable storage\\\" that cannot be lost in any failure-recovery scenario without potential consistency violations. There are two primary problems with this assumption. First, disk errors are the most common problem we\\n494:     observe in real operation of persistent data systems and they often do not leave data intact. Secondly, even if this were not a problem, we do not want to require the use of fsync on every write for our consistency\\n495:     guarantees as this can reduce performance by two to three orders of magnitude. The replicated log is one of the most basic primitives in distributed data systems, and there are many approaches for implementing one. A replicated log can be\n450:     used by other systems as a primitive for implementing other distributed systems in the <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_machine_replication\">state-machine style</a>.\n451:     <p>\n452: ","endLine":452,"startLine":449},{"content":"446: \n447:     <h4><a id=\"design_replicatedlog\" href=\"#design_replicatedlog\">Replicated Logs: Quorums, ISRs, and State Machines (Oh my!)</a></h4>\n448: \n449: ","endLine":449,"startLine":446},{"content":"493:     \"stable storage\" that cannot be lost in any failure-recovery scenario without potential consistency violations. There are two primary problems with this assumption. First, disk errors are the most common problem we\n494:     observe in real operation of persistent data systems and they often do not leave data intact. Secondly, even if this were not a problem, we do not want to require the use of fsync on every write for our consistency\n495:     guarantees as this can reduce performance by two to three orders of magnitude. Our protocol for allowing a replica to rejoin the ISR ensures that before rejoining, it must fully re-sync again even if it lost unflushed\n496:     data in its crash.\n497: coordinator's state machine is implemented across multiple Java files in the group-coordinator module. The state machine handles three main group types: Classic Groups, Consumer Groups (modern protocol), and Streams Groups.\\n\\n## State Definitions\\n\\n**Classic Groups** (legacy protocol): The state machine is defined in `ClassicGroupState.java` and includes five states:\\n- EMPTY: Group has no members\\n- PREPARING_REBALANCE: Group is preparing to rebalance (Join phase)\\n- COMPLETING_REBALANCE: Group awaits state assignment from leader (Sync phase)\\n- STABLE: Group is stable\\n- DEAD: Group is being removed\\n\\nTransitions are validated through the `validPreviousStates()` method in `ClassicGroupState.java`, which enforces state machine rules like: EMPTY → PREPARING_REBALANCE → COMPLETING_REBALANCE → STABLE.\\n\\n**Modern Consumer Groups**: Defined in `ConsumerGroup.java` with states:\\n- EMPTY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, DEAD\\n\\nMember-level states are in `MemberState.java`:\\n- STABLE: Member is reconciled with target assignment\\n- UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS: Member must revoke partitions\\n- UNRELEASED_PARTITIONS: Member waits for partitions to be released\\n\\n**Streams Groups**: Defined in `StreamsGroup.java` with states:\\n- EMPTY, NOT_READY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, DEAD\\n\\n**Share Groups**: Defined in `ShareGroup.java` with states:\\n- EMPTY, STABLE, DEAD\\n\\n## State Transition Logic\\n\\nThe primary state transitions occur through three main API calls:\\n\\n1. **Join Phase** (`classicGroupJoin` in `GroupMetadataManager.java`): Members join the group, triggering transition to PREPARING_REBALANCE state. Handled by:\\n   - `GroupCoordinator.joinGroup()` interface\\n   - `GroupCoordinatorService.joinGroup()` implementation\\n   - `GroupCoordinatorShard.classicGroupJoin()` routing\\n   - `GroupMetadataManager.classicGroupJoin()` logic\\n   - `ClassicGroup.transitionTo(PREPARING_REBALANCE)`\\n\\n2. **Sync Phase** (`classicGroupSync` in `GroupMetadataManager.java`): Leader provides assignment, triggering transition to COMPLETING_REBALANCE then STABLE. Handled by:\\n   - `GroupCoordinator.syncGroup()` interface\\n   - `GroupCoordinatorService.syncGroup()` implementation\\n   - `GroupCoordinatorShard.classicGroupSync()` routing\\n   - `GroupMetadataManager.classicGroupSync()` logic\\n   - `ClassicGroup.transitionTo(COMPLETING_REBALANCE)` then `transitionTo(STABLE)`\\n\\n3. **Rebalance** (triggered by membership changes): Detected through heartbeats (`classicGroupHeartbeat`) and member timeouts, causing transition back to PREPARING_REBALANCE.\\n\\n## Key Implementation Files\\n\\n**State Definitions**:\\n- `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/ClassicGroupState.java` - Classic group states and valid transitions\\n- `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/consumer/ConsumerGroup.java` - Modern consumer group states\\n- `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/MemberState.java` - The state machine handles three main group types: Classic Groups, Consumer Groups (modern protocol), and Streams Groups.\\n\\n## State Definitions\\n\\n**Classic Groups** (legacy protocol): The state machine is defined in `ClassicGroupState.java` and includes five states:\\n- EMPTY: Group has no members\\n- PREPARING_REBALANCE: Group is preparing to rebalance (Join phase)\\n- COMPLETING_REBALANCE: Group awaits state assignment from leader (Sync phase)\\n- STABLE: Group is stable\\n- DEAD: Group is being removed\\n\\nTransitions are validated through the `validPreviousStates()` method in `ClassicGroupState.java`, which enforces state machine rules like: EMPTY → PREPARING_REBALANCE → COMPLETING_REBALANCE → STABLE.\\n\\n**Modern Consumer Groups**: Defined in `ConsumerGroup.java` with states:\\n- EMPTY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, DEAD\\n\\nMember-level states are in `MemberState.java`:\\n- STABLE: Member is reconciled with target assignment\\n- UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS: Member must revoke partitions\\n- UNRELEASED_PARTITIONS: Member waits for partitions to be released\\n\\n**Streams Groups**: Defined in `StreamsGroup.java` with states:\\n- EMPTY, NOT_READY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, DEAD\\n\\n**Share Groups**: Defined in `ShareGroup.java` with states:\\n- EMPTY, STABLE, DEAD\\n\\n## State Transition Logic\\n\\nThe primary state transitions occur through three main API calls:\\n\\n1. **Join Phase** (`classicGroupJoin` in `GroupMetadataManager.java`): Members join the group, triggering transition to PREPARING_REBALANCE state. Handled by:\\n   - `GroupCoordinator.joinGroup()` interface\\n   - `GroupCoordinatorService.joinGroup()` implementation\\n   - `GroupCoordinatorShard.classicGroupJoin()` routing\\n   - `GroupMetadataManager.classicGroupJoin()` logic\\n   - `ClassicGroup.transitionTo(PREPARING_REBALANCE)`\\n\\n2. **Sync Phase** (`classicGroupSync` in `GroupMetadataManager.java`): Leader provides assignment, triggering transition to COMPLETING_REBALANCE then STABLE. Handled by:\\n   - `GroupCoordinator.syncGroup()` interface\\n   - `GroupCoordinatorService.syncGroup()` implementation\\n   - `GroupCoordinatorShard.classicGroupSync()` routing\\n   - `GroupMetadataManager.classicGroupSync()` logic\\n   - `ClassicGroup.transitionTo(COMPLETING_REBALANCE)` then `transitionTo(STABLE)`\\n\\n3. **Rebalance** (triggered by membership changes): Detected through heartbeats (`classicGroupHeartbeat`) and member timeouts, causing transition back to PREPARING_REBALANCE.\\n\\n## Key Implementation Files\\n\\n**State Definitions**:\\n- \"text\": \"The Apache Kafka consumer group coordinator's state machine is implemented across multiple Java files in the group-coordinator module. The state machine handles three main group types: Classic Groups, Consumer Groups (modern protocol), and Streams Groups.\\n\\n## State Definitions\\n\\n**Classic Groups** (legacy protocol): The state machine is defined in `ClassicGroupState.java` and includes five states:\\n- EMPTY: Group has no members\\n- PREPARING_REBALANCE: Group is preparing to rebalance (Join phase)\\n- COMPLETING_REBALANCE: Group awaits state assignment from leader (Sync phase)\\n- STABLE: Group is stable\\n- DEAD: Group is being removed\\n\\nTransitions are validated through the `validPreviousStates()` method in `ClassicGroupState.java`, which enforces state machine rules like: EMPTY → PREPARING_REBALANCE → COMPLETING_REBALANCE → STABLE.\\n\\n**Modern Consumer Groups**: Defined in `ConsumerGroup.java` with states:\\n- EMPTY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, DEAD\\n\\nMember-level states are in `MemberState.java`:\\n- STABLE: Member is reconciled with target assignment\\n- UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS: Member must revoke partitions\\n- UNRELEASED_PARTITIONS: Member waits for partitions to be released\\n\\n**Streams Groups**: Defined in `StreamsGroup.java` with states:\\n- EMPTY, NOT_READY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, DEAD\\n\\n**Share Groups**: Defined in `ShareGroup.java` with states:\\n- EMPTY, STABLE, DEAD\\n\\n## State Transition Logic\\n\\nThe primary state transitions occur through three main API calls:\\n\\n1. **Join Phase** (`classicGroupJoin` in `GroupMetadataManager.java`): Members join the group, triggering transition to PREPARING_REBALANCE state. Handled by:\\n   - `GroupCoordinator.joinGroup()` interface\\n   - `GroupCoordinatorService.joinGroup()` implementation\\n   - `GroupCoordinatorShard.classicGroupJoin()` routing\\n   - `GroupMetadataManager.classicGroupJoin()` logic\\n   - `ClassicGroup.transitionTo(PREPARING_REBALANCE)`\\n\\n2. **Sync Phase** (`classicGroupSync` in `GroupMetadataManager.java`): Leader provides assignment, triggering transition to COMPLETING_REBALANCE then STABLE. Handled by:\\n   - `GroupCoordinator.syncGroup()` interface\\n   - `GroupCoordinatorService.syncGroup()` implementation\\n   - `GroupCoordinatorShard.classicGroupSync()` routing\\n   - `GroupMetadataManager.classicGroupSync()` logic\\n   - `ClassicGroup.transitionTo(COMPLETING_REBALANCE)` then `transitionTo(STABLE)`\\n\\n3. **Rebalance** (triggered by membership changes): Detected through heartbeats (`classicGroupHeartbeat`) and member timeouts, causing transition back to PREPARING_REBALANCE.\\n\\n## Key Implementation Files\\n\\n**State Definitions**:\\n- `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/ClassicGroupState.java` - Classic group states and valid transitions\\n- `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/consumer/ConsumerGroup.java` - Modern consumer group states\\n- `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/MemberState.java` - Share group states\\n\\n**Transition Orchestration**:\\n- `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/ClassicGroup.java` - Implements `transitionTo()` and `assertValidTransition()` methods\\n- `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupMetadataManager.java` - Service-level implementation\\n- `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinator.java` - Public interface definition\\n\\n**Assignment Builders** (for state machine reconciliation):\\n- `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/consumer/CurrentAssignmentBuilder.java` -
